## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) ŌĆö nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear harmonic oscillator models. Common structures include restoring-force terms in x, damping terms in v, and optional time-dependent or periodic forcing terms in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear spring (simple harmonic oscillator in state-space): dv_dt = -c0 * x (undamped, unforced oscillator)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized spring-damper)
- Constant bias / gravity-like offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (equilibrium shift / constant acceleration)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * Abs(v) * v (drag-dominated dissipation)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip approximation away from vŌēł0)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order stiffness expansion: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (polynomial restoring force from potential expansion)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (alternative self-excitation mechanism)
- Nonlinear position-dependent damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (damping that increases with displacement)
- External harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven oscillator)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance, bistability)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type stiffness modulation): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric resonance / stability tongues)
- Nonlinear coupling term (geometric/nonlinear inertia surrogate): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x * v (energy transfer between states / nonconservative coupling)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * v (modulated dissipation / active control)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force from a potential: if dv_dt depends mainly on x with odd powers (x, x**3, x**5), it often indicates a conservative spring with symmetric potential energy.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: positive cubic stiffness term (e.g., -c * x**3 with c>0) typically hardens (frequency increases with amplitude), while the opposite sign softens (frequency decreases).
- Energy dissipation signature: terms proportional to v remove energy (viscous), while terms like -Abs(v)*v indicate high-speed drag; sign(v) indicates dry friction and can create non-smooth dynamics.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: damping that changes sign with amplitude (e.g., (c0 - c1*x**2)*v or (c0 - c1*v**2)*v) points to stable oscillations without external forcing.
- Periodic forcing identification: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms imply direct driving; resonance phenomena occur when the forcing frequency matches the natural frequency implied by the linear x term.
- Parametric resonance identification: multiplicative modulation (cos(c*t)*x) indicates time-varying stiffness, producing instability bands even without additive forcing.
- Equilibrium shift: a constant offset in dv_dt ( +c ) implies the equilibrium position is displaced; in data this appears as nonzero mean acceleration at xŌēł0,vŌēł0.
- Nonconservative cross-coupling: terms like x*v (or other mixed products) can indicate geometric nonlinearities, actuator effects, or coordinate-dependent damping/inertia approximations.
- Time-varying dissipation/control: modulation of the v coefficient by sin(c*t) suggests active control or environment changes that periodically alter damping.

4. `sin(v)` (coefficient Ōēł -0.196)

Key observations:
- The GT has `sin(v)` and `v*sin(x)` terms
- No polynomial-only expression can match the GT exactly (due to `sin` terms)
- Candidates with `sin(v)` or terms that can produce `sin(v)` might match
- `sin(c*v + c)` can represent `sin(v)` by setting appropriate constants

Let me check which candidates have `sin` terms:
- Candidates 1, 2, 3, 4, 32, 43, 44: have `sin(c*v + c)` type terms

But the GT needs BOTH `sin(v)` AND `v*sin(x)`. The term `sin(c*v+c)` can only give `sin(v)` (or a phase-shifted version). None of these candidates have `v*sin(x)`.

**No candidate has `v*sin(x)` as a basis function.** This means no candidate can exactly match the GT.

However, let me reconsider: could any candidate approximate `v*sin(x)` exactly using polynomial terms? Since `sin(x) = x - x┬│/6 + xŌüĄ/120 - ...`, we have `v*sin(x) = v*x - v*x┬│/6 + v*xŌüĄ/120 - ...`. This is an infinite series, so a finite polynomial can NEVER exactly equal `v*sin(x)`. By Rule 2, no approximations are allowed.

Let me verify candidates with `sin` terms more carefully:

**Candidates 1, 2, 3, 4, 32**: These have `sin(c*v+c)` which can give `sin(v)`, plus polynomial terms like `v*x`, `v*x┬│`, `v*xŌüĄ`. But `v*sin(x)` cannot be exactly represented by `v*x + v*x┬│ + v*xŌüĄ` (finite polynomial in x times v).

**Candidate 43**: `c0*x┬│ + c1 + c2*sin(c3*v+c4) + c5*v┬│ + c6*v*x + c7*v*x┬│` - same issue, no `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidate 44**: `c0*x┬│ + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v+c4) + c5*v┬│ + c6*vŌüĄ + c7*v*x + c8*v*x┬│` - same issue.

For ALL candidates: None contain `v*sin(x)` or any mechanism to produce it exactly. The `v*sin(x)` term in the GT is a product of `v` with `sin(x)`, which is a fundamentally different basis function from any polynomial term. By Rule 3 (linear independence), no finite combination of polynomial terms can equal `sin(x)`.

Therefore, **no candidate matches**.
